<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dell_facilities">Dell facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Dell facilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dell's headquarters is located in <a href="/wiki/Round_Rock,_Texas" title="Round Rock, Texas">Round Rock, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the company employed about 14,000 people in central Texas and was the region's largest private employer,<sup id="cite_ref-AS_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AS-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> which has 2,100,000 square feet (200,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenHQ_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenHQ-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> As of 1999 almost half of the general fund of the city of Round Rock originated from sales taxes generated from the Dell headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell previously had its headquarters in the <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">Arboretum</a> complex in northern Austin, Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-PopeDis_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopeDis-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> In 1989 Dell occupied 127,000 square feet (11,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) in the Arboretum complex.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, Dell had 1,200 employees in its headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-PopeDis_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopeDis-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, Dell submitted a document to Round Rock officials, titled "Dell Computer Corporate Headquarters, Round Rock, Texas, May 1993 Schematic Design." Despite the filing, during that year the company said that it was not going to move its headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, Dell announced that it was moving most of its employees out of the Arboretum, but that it was going to continue to occupy the top floor of the Arboretum and that the company's official headquarters address would continue to be the Arboretum. The top floor continued to hold Dell's board room, demonstration center, and visitor meeting room. Less than one month prior to August 29, 1994, Dell moved 1,100 customer support and telephone sales employees to Round Rock.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Dell's lease in the Arboretum had been scheduled to expire in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dell_diamond2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Dell_diamond2.jpg/220px-Dell_diamond2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="95" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Dell_diamond2.jpg/330px-Dell_diamond2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Dell_diamond2.jpg/440px-Dell_diamond2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1224" data-file-height="527" /></a><figcaption>The company sponsors <a href="/wiki/Dell_Diamond" title="Dell Diamond">Dell Diamond</a>, the home stadium of the <a href="/wiki/Round_Rock_Express" title="Round Rock Express">Round Rock Express</a>, the AAA <a href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor league baseball">minor league baseball</a> affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> major league baseball team.</figcaption></figure>
<p>By 1996, Dell was moving its headquarters to Round Rock.<sup id="cite_ref-HQMoving_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQMoving-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> As of January 1996, 3,500 people still worked at the current Dell headquarters. One building of the Round Rock headquarters, Round Rock 3, had space for 6,400 employees and was scheduled to be completed in November 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In 1998 Dell announced that it was going to add two buildings to its Round Rock complex, adding 1,600,000 square feet (150,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of office space to the complex.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, Dell announced that it would lease 80,000 square feet (7,400&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space in the <a href="/wiki/Las_Cimas" title="Las Cimas">Las Cimas</a> office complex in <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated</a> <a href="/wiki/Travis_County,_Texas" title="Travis County, Texas">Travis County, Texas</a>, between Austin and <a href="/wiki/West_Lake_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="West Lake Hills">West Lake Hills</a>, to house the company's executive offices and corporate headquarters. 100 senior executives were scheduled to work in the building by the end of 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In January 2001, the company leased the space in Las Cimas 2, located along <a href="/wiki/Loop_360" class="mw-redirect" title="Loop 360">Loop 360</a>. Las Cimas 2 housed Dell's executives, the investment operations, and some corporate functions. Dell also had an option for 138,000 square feet (12,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space in Las Cimas 3.<sup id="cite_ref-Subleaselascimas_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subleaselascimas-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> After a slowdown in business required reducing employees and production capacity, Dell decided to sublease its offices in two buildings in the Las Cimas office complex.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> In 2002 Dell announced that it planned to sublease its space to another tenant; the company planned to move its headquarters back to Round Rock once a tenant was secured.<sup id="cite_ref-Subleaselascimas_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subleaselascimas-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> By 2003, Dell moved its headquarters back to Round Rock. It leased all of Las Cimas I and II, with a total of 312,000 square feet (29,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), for about a seven-year period after 2003. By that year roughly 100,000 square feet (9,300&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of that space was absorbed by new subtenants.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Dell switched the power sources of the Round Rock headquarters to more environmentally friendly ones, with 60% of the total power coming from <a href="/wiki/TXU_Energy" title="TXU Energy">TXU Energy</a> wind farms and 40% coming from the Austin Community Landfill gas-to-energy plant operated by <a href="/wiki/Waste_Management,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Waste Management, Inc.">Waste Management, Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-GreenHQ_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenHQ-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell facilities in the United States are located in Austin, Texas; <a href="/wiki/Nashua,_New_Hampshire" title="Nashua, New Hampshire">Nashua, New Hampshire</a>; <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a>; <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a>, Oklahoma; <a href="/wiki/Peoria,_Illinois" title="Peoria, Illinois">Peoria, Illinois</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hillsboro,_Oregon" title="Hillsboro, Oregon">Hillsboro, Oregon</a> (Portland area); <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem, North Carolina</a>; <a href="/wiki/Eden_Prairie,_Minnesota" title="Eden Prairie, Minnesota">Eden Prairie, Minnesota</a> (<a href="/wiki/Compellent" class="mw-redirect" title="Compellent">Dell Compellent</a>); <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green,_Kentucky" title="Bowling Green, Kentucky">Bowling Green, Kentucky</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln, Nebraska</a>; and Miami, Florida. Facilities located abroad include <a href="/wiki/Penang,_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="Penang, Malaysia">Penang, Malaysia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Xiamen" title="Xiamen">Xiamen</a>, China; <a href="/wiki/Bracknell" title="Bracknell">Bracknell</a>, UK; <a href="/wiki/Manila,_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Manila, Philippines">Manila, Philippines</a><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chennai,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Chennai, India">Chennai, India</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad, India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Noida,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Noida, India">Noida, India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hortol%C3%A2ndia" title="Hortolândia">Hortolândia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, Brazil; <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, Slovakia; <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="Łódź">Łódź, Poland</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Panama City, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>; <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limerick" title="Limerick">Limerick</a>, Ireland; <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>, Morocco and Montpellier, France.
</p><p>The US and India are the only countries that have all Dell's business functions and provide support globally: research and development, manufacturing, finance, analysis, and customer care.<sup id="cite_ref-tech.fortune.cnn.com_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech.fortune.cnn.com-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Manufacturing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From its early beginnings, Dell operated as a pioneer in the "configure to order" approach to manufacturing—delivering individual PCs configured to customer specifications. In contrast, most PC manufacturers in those times delivered large orders to intermediaries on a quarterly basis.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To minimize the delay between purchase and delivery, Dell has a general policy of manufacturing its products close to its customers. This also allows for implementing a <a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_(business)" class="mw-redirect" title="Just-in-time (business)">just-in-time</a> (JIT) manufacturing approach, which minimizes <a href="/wiki/Inventory" title="Inventory">inventory</a> costs. Low inventory is another signature of the Dell business model—a critical consideration in an industry where components depreciate very rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell's manufacturing process covers assembly, software installation, functional testing (including "burn-in"), and quality control. Throughout most of the company's history, Dell manufactured desktop machines in-house and contracted out the manufacturing of base notebooks for configuration in-house.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The company's approach has changed, as cited in the 2006 Annual Report, which states, "We are continuing to expand our use of original design manufacturing partnerships and manufacturing outsourcing relationships." <i>The Wall Street Journal</i> reported in September 2008 that "Dell has approached contract computer manufacturers with offers to sell" their plants.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> By the late 2000s, Dell's "configure to order" approach of manufacturing—delivering individual PCs configured to customer specifications from its US facilities was no longer as efficient or competitive with high-volume Asian contract manufacturers as PCs became powerful low-cost commodities.<sup id="cite_ref-statesman1_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statesman1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Assembly of desktop computers for the North American market formerly took place at Dell plants in Austin, Texas, (original location) and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon,_Tennessee" title="Lebanon, Tennessee">Lebanon, Tennessee</a>, (opened in 1999), which were closed in 2008 and early 2009, respectively. The plant in <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem, North Carolina</a>, opened in 2005 but ceased operations in November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-theregister.co.uk_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theregister.co.uk-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bizjournals.com_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournals.com-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Most of the work that used to take place in Dell's US plants was transferred to contract manufacturers in Asia and Mexico, or some of Dell's own factories overseas. The <a href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami, Florida">Miami, Florida</a>, facility of its Alienware subsidiary remains in operation, while Dell continues to produce its servers (its most profitable products) in Austin, Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-statesman1_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statesman1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell assembled computers for the <a href="/wiki/Europe,_the_Middle_East_and_Africa" title="Europe, the Middle East and Africa">EMEA</a> market at the <a href="/wiki/Limerick" title="Limerick">Limerick</a> facility in the Republic of Ireland, and once employed about 4,500 people in that country. Dell began manufacturing in Limerick in 1991 and went on to become Ireland's largest exporter of goods and its second-largest company and foreign investor. On January 8, 2009, Dell announced that it would move all Dell manufacturing in Limerick to Dell's new plant in the Polish city of <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="Łódź">Łódź</a> by January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> officials said they would investigate a €52.7million aid package the Polish government used to attract Dell away from Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> European Manufacturing Facility 1 (EMF1, opened in 1990) and EMF3 form part of the <a href="/wiki/Raheen_Industrial_Estate" class="mw-redirect" title="Raheen Industrial Estate">Raheen Industrial Estate</a> near Limerick. EMF2 (previously a <a href="/wiki/Wang_Laboratories" title="Wang Laboratories">Wang</a> facility, later occupied by <a href="/wiki/Flextronics" class="mw-redirect" title="Flextronics">Flextronics</a>, situated in Castletroy) closed in 2002,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and Dell Inc. has consolidated production into EMF3 (EMF1 now<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2010)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> contains only offices).<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Subsidies from the Polish government did keep Dell for a long time.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> After ending assembly in the Limerick plant the <a href="/wiki/Cherrywood,_Dublin" title="Cherrywood, Dublin">Cherrywood</a> Technology Campus in Dublin was the largest Dell office in the republic with over 1200 people in sales (mainly UK &amp; Ireland), support (enterprise support for EMEA) and research and development for cloud computing, but no more manufacturing except<sup id="cite_ref-ida_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ida-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Dell's Alienware subsidiary, which manufactures PCs in an Athlone, Ireland, plant. Whether this facility will remain in Ireland is not certain.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Dell started production at EMF4 in Łódź, Poland, in late 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell moved desktop, notebook and PowerEdge server manufacturing for the South American market from the <a href="/wiki/Eldorado_do_Sul,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Eldorado do Sul, Brazil">Eldorado do Sul</a> plant opened in 1999, to a new plant in <a href="/wiki/Hortol%C3%A2ndia" title="Hortolândia">Hortolândia, Brazil</a>, in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Products"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope_and_brands">Scope and brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Scope and brands"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dell_wiki.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Dell_wiki.JPG/220px-Dell_wiki.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Dell_wiki.JPG/330px-Dell_wiki.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Dell_wiki.JPG/440px-Dell_wiki.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a><figcaption>Dell's tagline "Yours is Here", as seen at their <a href="/wiki/SM_Mall_of_Asia" title="SM Mall of Asia">Mall of Asia</a> branch in <a href="/wiki/Pasay" title="Pasay">Pasay</a>, Philippines</figcaption></figure>
<p>The corporation markets specific brand names to different <a href="/wiki/Market_segment" class="mw-redirect" title="Market segment">market segments</a>.
</p><p>Its Business/Corporate class includes:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dell_OptiPlex" title="Dell OptiPlex">OptiPlex</a> (office <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop computer</a> systems)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Dimension" title="Dell Dimension">Dimension</a> (home desktop computer systems)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Vostro" title="Dell Vostro">Vostro</a> (office/small business desktop and <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">notebook</a> systems)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_n_Series" title="Dell n Series">n Series</a> (desktop and notebook computers shipped with <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> or <a href="/wiki/FreeDOS" title="FreeDOS">FreeDOS</a> installed)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Latitude" title="Dell Latitude">Latitude</a> (business-focused notebooks)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Precision" title="Dell Precision">Precision</a> (<a href="/wiki/Computer_workstation" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer workstation">workstation</a> systems and high-performance "Mobile Workstation" notebooks),<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_PowerEdge" class="mw-redirect" title="Dell PowerEdge">PowerEdge</a> (business <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_PowerVault" title="Dell PowerVault">PowerVault</a> (direct-attach and <a href="/wiki/Network-attached_storage" title="Network-attached storage">network-attached storage</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Force10" title="Force10">Force10</a> (<a href="/wiki/Network_switch" title="Network switch">network switches</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_PowerConnect" title="Dell PowerConnect">PowerConnect</a> (<a href="/wiki/Network_switch" title="Network switch">network switches</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Compellent" class="mw-redirect" title="Dell Compellent">Dell Compellent</a> (<a href="/wiki/Storage_area_network" title="Storage area network">storage area networks</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EqualLogic" title="EqualLogic">EqualLogic</a> (enterprise class <a href="/wiki/ISCSI" title="ISCSI">iSCSI</a> <a href="/wiki/Storage_area_network" title="Storage area network">SANs</a>)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130123095422/http://content.dell.com/us/en/healthcare/healthcare-electronic-medical-records.aspx">Dell EMR</a> (electronic medical records)</li></ul>
<p>Dell's Home Office/Consumer class includes:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Inspiron" title="Dell Inspiron">Inspiron</a> (budget desktop and notebook computers)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_XPS" title="Dell XPS">XPS</a> (high-end desktop and notebook computers)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_G_Series" title="Dell G Series">G Series</a> (high/medium-performance gaming laptops)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alienware" title="Alienware">Alienware</a> (high-performance gaming systems)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dell_Venue" title="Dell Venue">Venue</a> (Tablets Android / Windows)</li></ul>
<p>Dell's Peripherals class includes <a href="/wiki/Keydrive" class="mw-redirect" title="Keydrive">USB keydrives</a>, <a href="/wiki/LCD_television" title="LCD television">LCD televisions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Printer_(computing)" title="Printer (computing)">printers</a>; Dell monitors includes <a href="/wiki/LCD" class="mw-redirect" title="LCD">LCD TVs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plasma_display" title="Plasma display">plasma TVs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_projector" title="Video projector">projectors</a> for <a href="/wiki/HDTV" class="mw-redirect" title="HDTV">HDTV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_display" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer display">monitors</a>. Dell UltraSharp is further a high-end brand of monitors.
</p><p>Dell service and support brands include the <i>Dell Solution Station</i> (extended domestic support services, previously "Dell on Call"), <i><a href="/wiki/Dell_Support_Center" title="Dell Support Center">Dell Support Center</a></i> (extended support services abroad), <i>Dell Business Support</i> (a commercial service-contract that provides an industry-certified technician with a lower call-volume than in normal queues), <i>Dell Everdream Desktop Management</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">Software as a service</a>" <a href="/wiki/Remote-desktop_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Remote-desktop management">remote-desktop management</a>, originally a SaaS company founded by <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>'s cousin, <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_Rive" title="Lyndon Rive">Lyndon Rive</a>, which Dell bought in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>), and <i>Your Tech Team</i> (a support-queue available to home users who purchased their systems either through Dell's website or through Dell phone-centers).
</p><p>Discontinued products and brands include <a href="/wiki/Dell_Axim" title="Dell Axim">Axim</a> (<a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">PDA</a>; discontinued April 9, 2007),<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dell_Dimension" title="Dell Dimension">Dimension</a> (home and small office desktop computers; discontinued July 2007), <a href="/wiki/Dell_Digital_Jukebox" title="Dell Digital Jukebox">Dell Digital Jukebox</a> (MP3 player; discontinued August 2006), Dell PowerApp (application-based servers), Dell Optiplex (desktop and tower computers previously supported to run server and desktop operating systems), Dell Unix (an <a href="/wiki/UNIX_System_V" title="UNIX System V">SVR4</a>-based Unix operating system for its Dell-branded PCs and workstations; discontinued in 1993) and Dell Mobile Connect（Windows Mobile application; discontinued July 31st, 2022).<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Security"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-signed_root_certificate">Self-signed root certificate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Self-signed root certificate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2015, it emerged that several Dell computers had shipped with an identical pre-installed <a href="/wiki/Root_certificate" title="Root certificate">root certificate</a> known as "eDellRoot".<sup id="cite_ref-ars-selfsigned_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-selfsigned-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> This raised such security risks as attackers impersonating <a href="/wiki/HTTPS" title="HTTPS">HTTPS</a>-protected websites such as <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> and malware being signed with the certificate to bypass Microsoft software filtering.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-selfsigned_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-selfsigned-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Dell apologized and offered a removal tool.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-removal_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-removal-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dell_Foundation_Services">Dell Foundation Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dell Foundation Services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Also in November 2015, a researcher discovered that customers with diagnostic program Dell Foundation Services could be digitally tracked using the unique service tag number assigned to them by the program.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-dfs_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-dfs-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> This was possible even if a customer enabled <a href="/wiki/Private_browsing" title="Private browsing">private browsing</a> and deleted their <a href="/wiki/Browser_cookie" class="mw-redirect" title="Browser cookie">browser cookies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-dfs_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-dfs-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a></i> recommended that Dell customers uninstall the program until the issue was addressed.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-dfs_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-dfs-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_aspects">Commercial aspects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Commercial aspects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Organization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The board consists of nine directors. Michael Dell, the founder of the company, serves as chairman of the board and chief executive officer. Other board members include <a href="/wiki/Donald_J._Carty" title="Donald J. Carty">Don Carty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judy_Lewent" title="Judy Lewent">Judy Lewent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Luft" title="Klaus Luft">Klaus Luft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_J._Mandl" title="Alex J. Mandl">Alex Mandl</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nunn" title="Sam Nunn">Sam Nunn</a>. <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">Shareholders</a> elect the nine board members at meetings, and those board members who do not get a majority of votes must submit a resignation to the board, which will subsequently choose whether or not to accept the resignation. The board of directors usually sets up five committees having oversight over specific matters. These committees include the Audit Committee, which handles accounting issues, including auditing and reporting; the Compensation Committee, which approves compensation for the CEO and other employees of the company; the Finance Committee, which handles financial matters such as proposed mergers and acquisitions; the Governance and Nominating Committee, which handles various corporate matters (including the nomination of the board); and the Antitrust Compliance Committee, which attempts to prevent company practices from violating <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> laws. <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Day-to-day operations of the company are run by the Global Executive Management Committee, which sets <a href="/wiki/Strategic_management" title="Strategic management">strategic direction</a>. Dell has regional senior vice-presidents for countries other than the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Marketing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dell advertisements have appeared in several types of media including television, the Internet, magazines, <a href="/wiki/Mail-order_catalog" class="mw-redirect" title="Mail-order catalog">catalogs</a>, and newspapers. Some of Dell Inc's marketing strategies include lowering prices at all times of the year, free bonus products (such as Dell printers), and free shipping to encourage more sales and stave off competitors. In 2006, Dell cut its prices in an effort to maintain its 19.2% market share. This also cut profit margins by more than half, from 8.7 to 4.3 percent. To maintain its low prices, Dell continues to accept most purchases of its products via the Internet and through the telephone network, and to move its customer-care division to India and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A popular United States television and print ad campaign in the early 2000s featured the actor <a href="/wiki/Ben_Curtis_(actor)" title="Ben Curtis (actor)">Ben Curtis</a> playing the part of "Steven", a lightly mischievous blond-haired youth who came to the assistance of bereft computer purchasers. Each television advertisement usually ended with Steven's catch-phrase: "Dude, you're gettin' a Dell!"<sup id="cite_ref-SlateDell_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SlateDell-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A subsequent advertising campaign featured <a href="/wiki/Intern" class="mw-redirect" title="Intern">interns</a> at Dell headquarters (with Curtis' character appearing in a small cameo at the end of one of the first commercials in this particular campaign).
</p><p>In 2007, Dell switched advertising agencies in the US from <a href="/wiki/BBDO" title="BBDO">BBDO</a> to <a href="/wiki/Working_Mother" title="Working Mother">Working Mother</a> Media. In July 2007, Dell released new advertising created by Working Mother to support the Inspiron and XPS lines. The ads featured music from the <a href="/wiki/The_Flaming_Lips" title="The Flaming Lips">Flaming Lips</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devo" title="Devo">Devo</a> who re-formed especially to record the song in the ad "Work it Out". Also in 2007, Dell began using the slogan "Yours is here" to say that it customizes computers to fit customers' requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-engadget_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-engadget-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in 2011, Dell began hosting a conference in Austin, Texas, at the Austin Convention Center titled "Dell World". The event featured new technology and services provided by Dell and Dell's partners. In 2011, the event was held October 12–14.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, the event was held December 11–13.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the event was held December 11–13.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, the event was held November 4–6.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dell_partner_program">Dell partner program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Dell partner program"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In late 2007, Dell Inc. announced that it planned to expand its program to <a href="/wiki/Value-added_reseller" title="Value-added reseller">value-added resellers</a> (VARs), giving it the official name of "Dell Partner Direct" and a new Website.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell India has started Online Ecommerce website<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> with its Dell Partner www.compuindia.com GNG Electronics Pvt Ltd<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> termed as Dell Express Ship Affiliate(DESA).
The main objective was to reduce the delivery time. Customers who visit Dell India official site are given the option to buy online which then will be redirected to Dell affiliate website compuindia.com.<sup id="cite_ref-tech.fortune.cnn.com_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech.fortune.cnn.com-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_analytics">Global analytics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Global analytics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Dell also operates a captive analytics division which supports pricing, web analytics, and supply chain operations. DGA operates as a single, centralized entity with a global view of Dell's business activities. The firm supports over 500 internal customers worldwide and has created a quantified impact of over $500 million.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms_of_marketing_of_laptop_security">Criticisms of marketing of laptop security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Criticisms of marketing of laptop security"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2008, Dell received press coverage over its claim of having the world's most secure laptops, specifically, its Latitude D630 and Latitude D830.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> At Lenovo's request, the (US) National Advertising Division (NAD) evaluated the claim, and reported that Dell did not have enough evidence to support it.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail">Retail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Retail"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dell first opened their retail stores in India.<sup id="cite_ref-tech.fortune.cnn.com_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech.fortune.cnn.com-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: United States"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the early 1990s, Dell sold its products through <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costco" title="Costco">Costco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam&#39;s Club">Sam's Club</a> stores in the United States. Dell stopped this practice in 1994, citing low profit margins on the business, exclusively distributing through a direct-sales model for the next decade. In 2003, Dell briefly sold products in <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> stores in the US. In 2007, Dell started shipping its products to major retailers in the US once again, starting with <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam&#39;s Club">Sam's Club</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Wal-Mart</a>. <a href="/wiki/Staples_Inc." title="Staples Inc.">Staples</a>, the largest office-supply retailer in the US, and <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, the largest electronics retailer in the US, became Dell retail partners later that same year.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Kiosks">Kiosks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Kiosks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Starting in 2002, Dell opened <a href="/wiki/Kiosk" title="Kiosk">kiosk</a> locations in the United States to allow customers to examine products before buying them directly from the company. Starting in 2005, Dell expanded <a href="/wiki/Kiosk" title="Kiosk">kiosk</a> locations to include shopping malls across Australia, Canada, Singapore and Hong Kong. On January 30, 2008, Dell announced it would shut down all 140 kiosks in the US due to expansion into retail stores.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> By June 3, 2010, Dell had also shut down all of its mall kiosks in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail_stores">Retail stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Retail stores"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of the end of February 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Dell products shipped to one of the largest office supply retailers in Canada, <a href="/wiki/Staples_Business_Depot" class="mw-redirect" title="Staples Business Depot">Staples Business Depot</a>. In April 2008, <a href="/wiki/Future_Shop" title="Future Shop">Future Shop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a> began carrying a subset of Dell products, such as certain desktops, laptops, printers, and monitors.
</p><p>Since some shoppers in certain markets show reluctance to purchase technological products through the phone or the Internet, Dell has looked into opening retail operations in some countries in Central Europe and Russia. In April 2007, Dell opened a retail store in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>. In October of the same year, Dell opened a retail store in Moscow.
</p><p>In the UK, <a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a>'s flagship <a href="/wiki/Trocadero_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trocadero (London)">Trocadero</a> store has sold Dell XPS PCs since December 2007. From January 2008 the UK stores of <a href="/wiki/DSG_International_(retailer)" class="mw-redirect" title="DSG International (retailer)">DSGi</a> have sold Dell products (in particular, through <a href="/wiki/Currys" title="Currys">Currys</a> and <a href="/wiki/PC_World_(retailer)" title="PC World (retailer)">PC World</a> stores). As of 2008, the large supermarket chain <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> has sold Dell laptops and desktops in outlets throughout the UK.
</p><p>In May 2008, Dell reached an agreement with the office supply chain, <a href="/wiki/Officeworks" title="Officeworks">Officeworks</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/Coles_Group" title="Coles Group">Coles Group</a>), to stock a few modified models in the Inspiron desktop and notebook range. These models have slightly different model numbers, but almost replicate the ones available from the Dell Store. Dell continued its retail push in the Australian market with its partnership with Harris Technology (another part of Coles Group) in November of the same year. In addition, Dell expanded its retail distributions in Australia through an agreement with the discount electrical retailer, <a href="/wiki/The_Good_Guys_(Australasia)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Good Guys (Australasia)">The Good Guys</a>, known for "Slashing Prices". Dell agreed to distribute a variety of makes of both desktops and notebooks, including <a href="/wiki/Studio" title="Studio">Studio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dell_XPS" title="Dell XPS">XPS</a> systems in late 2008. Dell and <a href="/wiki/Dick_Smith_Electronics" class="mw-redirect" title="Dick Smith Electronics">Dick Smith Electronics</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/Woolworths_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Woolworths Limited">Woolworths Limited</a>) reached an agreement to expand within Dick Smith's 400 stores throughout Australia and New Zealand in May 2009 (1 year since Officeworks—owned by Coles Group—reached a deal). The retailer has agreed to distribute a variety of <a href="/wiki/Inspiron" class="mw-redirect" title="Inspiron">Inspiron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Studio" title="Studio">Studio</a> notebooks, with minimal Studio desktops from the Dell range. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Dell continues to run and operate its various kiosks in 18 shopping centers throughout Australia. On March 31, 2010, Dell announced to Australian Kiosk employees that they were shutting down the Australian/New Zealand Dell kiosk program.
</p><p>In Germany, Dell is selling selected smartphones and notebooks via <a href="/wiki/Media_Markt" class="mw-redirect" title="Media Markt">Media Markt</a> and Saturn, as well as some shopping websites.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Competition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dell's major competitors include <a href="/wiki/Lenovo" title="Lenovo">Lenovo</a>, Hewlett-Packard (HP), <a href="/wiki/Hasee" title="Hasee">Hasee</a>, Acer, <a href="/wiki/Fujitsu" title="Fujitsu">Fujitsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gateway,_Inc." title="Gateway, Inc.">Gateway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, Asus, <a href="/wiki/Micro-Star_International" title="Micro-Star International">MSI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> and Apple. Dell and its subsidiary, Alienware, compete in the enthusiast market against AVADirect, <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Northwest" title="Falcon Northwest">Falcon Northwest</a>, <a href="/wiki/VoodooPC" title="VoodooPC">VoodooPC</a> (a subsidiary of HP), and other manufacturers. In the second quarter of 2006, Dell had between 18% and 19% share of the worldwide personal computer market, compared to HP with roughly 15%.
</p><p>In late 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Dell lost its lead in the PC business to Hewlett-Packard. Both <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Data_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Data Corporation">IDC</a> estimated that in the third quarter of 2006, HP shipped more units<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> worldwide than Dell did. Dell's 3.6% growth paled in comparison to HP's 15% growth during the same period. The problem got worse in the fourth quarter, when Gartner estimated<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> that Dell PC shipments declined 8.9% (versus HP's 23.9% growth). As a result, at the end of 2006 Dell's overall PC market share stood at 13.9% (versus HP's 17.4%).
</p><p>IDC reported that Dell lost more server market share than any of the top four competitors in that arena. IDC's Q4 2006 estimates show Dell's share of the server market at 8.1%, down from 9.5% in the previous year. This represents an 8.8% loss year-over-year, primarily to competitors <a href="/wiki/EMC_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="EMC Corporation">EMC</a> and IBM. As of 2021, Dell is the third-largest PC manufacturer after Lenovo and HP.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnership_with_EMC">Partnership with EMC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Partnership with EMC"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2001, Dell and EMC entered into a partnership whereby both companies jointly design products, and Dell provided support for certain EMC products including midrange storage systems, such as <a href="/wiki/Fibre_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fibre channel">fibre channel</a> and <a href="/wiki/ISCSI" title="ISCSI">iSCSI</a> <a href="/wiki/Storage_area_network" title="Storage area network">storage area networks</a>. The relationship also promotes and sells OEM versions of backup, recovery, replication and archiving software.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> On December 9, 2008, Dell and EMC announced the multi-year extension, through 2013, of the strategic partnership with EMC. In addition, Dell expanded its product lineup by adding the EMC Celerra NX4 storage system to the portfolio of Dell/EMC family of networked storage systems and partnered on a new line of <a href="/wiki/Data_deduplication" title="Data deduplication">data deduplication</a> products as part of its TierDisk family of <a href="/wiki/Data_storage_device" class="mw-redirect" title="Data storage device">data storage devices</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 17, 2011, Dell discontinued reselling all EMC storage products, ending the partnership 2 years early.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Later Dell would acquire and merge with EMC in the largest tech merger to date.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Environmental record"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dell committed to reducing greenhouse gas emissions from its global activities by 40% by 2015, with the 2008 fiscal year as the baseline year.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> It is listed in <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>'s Guide to Greener Electronics that scores leading electronics manufacturers according to their policies on sustainability, <a href="/wiki/Climate_and_energy" title="Climate and energy">climate and energy</a> and how green their products are. In November 2011, Dell ranked 2nd out of 15 listed electronics makers (increasing its score to 5.1 from 4.9, which it gained in the previous ranking from October 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dell was the first company to publicly state a timeline for the elimination of toxic polyvinyl chloride (PVC) and brominated flame retardants (BFRs), which it planned to phase out by the end of 2009. It revised this commitment and now aims to remove toxics by the end of 2011 but only in its computing products.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
In March 2010, Greenpeace activists protested at Dell offices in Bangalore, Amsterdam and Copenhagen calling for Dell's founder and CEO Michael Dell to "drop the toxics" and claiming that Dell's aspiration to be 'the greenest technology company on the planet'<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> was "hypocritical".<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Dell has launched its first products completely free of PVC and BFRs with the G-Series monitors (G2210 and G2410) in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In its 2012 report on progress relating to <a href="/wiki/Conflict_minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Conflict minerals">conflict minerals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Enough_Project" title="Enough Project">Enough Project</a> rated Dell the eighth-highest of 24 consumer electronics companies.<sup id="cite_ref-EnoughProject2012_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnoughProject2012-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_initiatives">Green initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Green initiatives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dell became the first company in the <a href="/wiki/Information_technology_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Information technology industry">information technology industry</a> to establish a product-<a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> goal (in 2004) and completed the implementation of its global consumer recycling-program in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
On February 6, 2007, the National Recycling Coalition awarded Dell its "Recycling Works" award for efforts to promote producer responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Recycling_Coalition_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Recycling_Coalition-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
On July 19, 2007, Dell announced that it had exceeded targets in working to achieve a multi-year goal of recovering 275 million pounds of computer equipment by 2009. The company reported the recovery of 78 million pounds (nearly 40,000 tons) of IT equipment from customers in 2006, a 93-percent increase over 2005; and 12.4% of the equipment Dell sold seven years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-Dell_Inc._251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dell_Inc.-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 5, 2007, Dell set a goal of becoming the greenest technology company on Earth for the long term.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The company launched a <a href="/wiki/Zero-carbon" class="mw-redirect" title="Zero-carbon">zero-carbon</a> initiative that includes:
</p>
<ol><li>reducing Dell's <a href="/wiki/Carbon_intensity" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon intensity">carbon intensity</a> by 15 percent by 2012</li>
<li>requiring primary suppliers to report carbon emissions data during quarterly business reviews</li>
<li>partnering with customers to build the "greenest PC on the planet"</li>
<li>expanding the company's carbon-offsetting program, "Plant a Tree for Me"</li></ol>
<p>Dell reports its environmental performance in an annual <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Social_Responsibility" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate Social Responsibility">Corporate Social Responsibility</a> (CSR) Report that follows the <a href="/wiki/Global_Reporting_Initiative" title="Global Reporting Initiative">Global Reporting Initiative</a> (GRI) protocol. Dell's 2008 CSR report ranked as "Application Level B" as "checked by GRI".<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The company aims to reduce its external environmental impact through an energy-efficient evolution of products, and also reduce its direct operational impact through energy-efficiency programs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Criticism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Lawsuits_involving_Dell_Inc." title="Lawsuits involving Dell Inc.">Lawsuits involving Dell Inc.</a></div>
<p>In the 1990s, Dell switched from using primarily <a href="/wiki/ATX" title="ATX">ATX</a> <a href="/wiki/Motherboard" title="Motherboard">motherboards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_power_supply" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer power supply">PSU</a> to using boards and power supplies with mechanically identical but differently wired connectors. This meant customers wishing to upgrade their hardware would have to replace parts with scarce Dell-compatible parts instead of commonly available parts. While motherboard power connections reverted to the industry standard in 2003, Dell remains secretive about their motherboard pin-outs for peripherals (such as MMC readers and power on/off switches and LEDs).<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, complaints about Dell more than doubled to 1,533, after earnings grew 52% that year.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, Dell acknowledged that it had problems with customer service. Issues included call transfers<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
of more than 45% of calls and long wait times. Dell's <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blog</a> detailed the response: "We're spending more than a $100&#160;million—and a lot of blood, sweat, and tears of talented people—to fix this."<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Later in the year, the company increased its spending on customer service to $150&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Since 2018, Dell has seen significant increase in consumer satisfaction. Moreover, their customer service has been praised for its prompt and accurate answers to most questions, especially those directed to their social media support.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 17, 2007, Dell Inc. announced that after an internal investigation into its accounting practices it would restate and reduce earnings from 2003 through to the first quarter of 2007 by a total amount of between $50&#160;million and $150&#160;million, or 2 cents to 7 cents per share.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> The investigation, begun in November 2006, resulted from concerns raised by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> over some documents and information that Dell Inc. had submitted.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> It was alleged that Dell had not disclosed large exclusivity payments received from <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> for agreeing not to buy processors from rival manufacturer <a href="/wiki/AMD" title="AMD">AMD</a>. In 2010 Dell finally paid $100&#160;million (equivalent to $136,400,000&#32;in 2023) to settle the SEC's charges of fraud. Michael Dell and other executives also paid penalties and suffered other sanctions, without admitting or denying the charges.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2009, Dell apologized after drawing the ire of the Taiwanese Consumer Protection Commission for twice refusing to honor a flood of orders against unusually low prices offered on its Taiwanese website. In the first instance, Dell offered a 19" LCD panel for $15. In the second instance, Dell offered its Latitude E4300 notebook at NT$18,558 (US$580), 70% lower than the usual price of NT$60,900 (US$1900). Concerning the E4300, rather than honor the discount taking a significant loss, the firm withdrew orders and offered a voucher of up to NT$20,000 (US$625) a customer in compensation. The consumer rights authorities in Taiwan fined Dell NT$1&#160;million (US$31250) for customer rights infringements. Many consumers sued the firm for unfair compensation. A court in southern Taiwan ordered the firm to deliver 18 laptops and 76 flat-panel monitors to 31 consumers for NT$490,000 (US$15,120), less than a third of the normal price.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> The court said the event could hardly be regarded as mistakes, as the prestigious firm said the company mispriced its products twice in Taiwanese website within 3 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Michael Dell made a $24.4 billion buyout bid in August 2013 (equivalent to $31,470,000,000&#32;in 2023), activist shareholder <a href="/wiki/Carl_Icahn" title="Carl Icahn">Carl Icahn</a> sued the company and its board in an attempt to derail the bid and promote his own forthcoming offer.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Strategic_Policy_Institute" title="Australian Strategic Policy Institute">Australian Strategic Policy Institute</a> accused at least 82 major brands, including Dell, of being connected to forced <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">Uyghur</a> labor in <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
